In the latter case, the seed coat protects the seed from <a href="/wiki/Digestion" title="Digestion">digestion</a>, while often weakening the seed coat such that the embryo is ready to sprout when it is deposited, along with a bit of fecal matter that acts as fertilizer, far from the parent plant.  <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">Microorganisms</a> are often effective in breaking down hard seed coats and are sometimes used by people as a treatment; the seeds are stored in a moist warm sandy medium for several months under nonsterile conditions.
</p><p><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stratification_(botany)" title="Stratification (botany)">Stratification</a></b>, also called moist-chilling, breaks down physiological dormancy, and involves the addition of moisture to the seeds so they absorb water, and they are then subjected to a period of moist chilling to after-ripen the embryo. Sowing in late summer and fall and allowing to overwinter under cool conditions is an effective way to stratify seeds; some seeds respond more favorably to periods of oscillating temperatures which are a part of the natural environment.
</p><p><b>Leaching</b> or the soaking in water removes chemical inhibitors in some seeds that prevent germination. <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">Rain</a> and melting <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snow</a> naturally accomplish this task. For seeds planted in gardens, running water is best – if soaked in a container, 12 to 24 hours of soaking is sufficient. Soaking longer, especially in stagnant water, can result in oxygen starvation and seed death. Seeds with hard seed coats can be soaked in hot water to break open the impermeable cell layers that prevent water intake.
</p><p>Other methods used to assist in the germination of seeds that have dormancy include prechilling, predrying, daily alternation of temperature, light exposure, potassium nitrate, the use of plant growth regulators, such as gibberellins, cytokinins, ethylene, thiourea, sodium hypochlorite, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Some seeds germinate best after a fire. For some seeds, fire cracks hard seed coats, while in others, chemical dormancy is broken in reaction to the presence of smoke. Liquid smoke is often used by gardeners to assist in the germination of these species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sterile_seeds">Sterile seeds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sterile seeds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seeds may be sterile for few reasons: they may have been irradiated, unpollinated, cells lived past expectancy, or bred for the purpose.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution_and_origin_of_seeds">Evolution and origin of seeds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Evolution and origin of seeds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The issue of the origin of seed plants remains unsolved. However, more and more data tends to place this origin in the middle <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a>. The description in 2004 of the proto-seed <i>Runcaria heinzelinii</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Givetian" title="Givetian">Givetian</a> of <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> is an indication of that ancient origin of seed-plants. As with modern ferns, most land plants before this time reproduced by sending into the air <a href="/wiki/Spore" title="Spore">spores</a> that would land and become whole new plants.
</p><p>Taxonomists have described early "true" seeds from the upper Devonian, which probably became the theater of their true first <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_radiation" title="Evolutionary radiation">evolutionary radiation</a>. With this radiation came an <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_seed_size" title="Evolution of seed size">evolution of seed size</a>, shape, dispersal and eventually the radiation of gymnosperms and angiosperms and <a href="/wiki/Monocotyledon" title="Monocotyledon">monocotyledons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dicotyledon" title="Dicotyledon">dicotyledons</a>. Seed plants progressively became one of the major elements of nearly all ecosystems.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="True_to_the_seed">True to the seed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: True to the seed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Also called growing true, refers to plants whose seed will yield the same type of plant as the original plant. Open pollinated plants, which include heirlooms, will almost always grow true to seed if another variety does not cross-pollinate them.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seed_microbiome">Seed microbiome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Seed microbiome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Microbiome_inheritance.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1080" decoding="async" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Microbiome_inheritance.gif/325px-Microbiome_inheritance.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Microbiome_inheritance.gif/488px-Microbiome_inheritance.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Microbiome_inheritance.gif/650px-Microbiome_inheritance.gif 2x" width="325"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Microbiome_inheritance.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Microbial transmission from seed to seedling<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onlinelibrary.wiley.com_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-onlinelibrary.wiley.com-52">[52]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Seeds harbor a diverse microbial community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Most of these microorganisms are transmitted from the seed to the developing seedlings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onlinelibrary.wiley.com_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-onlinelibrary.wiley.com-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_importance">Economic importance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economic importance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phaseolus_vulgaris_seed.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="168" data-file-width="252" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Phaseolus_vulgaris_seed.jpg/220px-Phaseolus_vulgaris_seed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Phaseolus_vulgaris_seed.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phaseolus_vulgaris_seed.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Phaseolus_vulgaris" title="Phaseolus vulgaris">Phaseolus vulgaris</a></i> (common bean or green bean) seeds are diverse in size, shape, and color.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seed_market">Seed market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Seed market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the United States farmers spent $22 billion on seeds in 2018, a 35 percent increase since 2010. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DowDuPont" title="DowDuPont">DowDuPont</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monsanto" title="Monsanto">Monsanto</a> account for 72 percent of corn and soybean seed sales in the U.S. with the average price of a bag of GMO <a href="/wiki/Sweet_corn" title="Sweet corn">corn</a> seed is priced at $270.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Edible_seeds">Edible seeds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Edible seeds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_edible_seeds" title="List of edible seeds">List of edible seeds</a></div>
<p>Many seeds are edible and the majority of human calories comes from seeds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> especially from <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">cereals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">nuts</a>. Seeds also provide most <a href="/wiki/Cooking_oil" title="Cooking oil">cooking oils</a>, many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beverage" title="Beverage">beverages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spices</a> and some important <a href="/wiki/Food_additive" title="Food additive">food additives</a>.  In different seeds the <a href="/wiki/Embryo#Embryos_of_plants_and_animals" title="Embryo">seed embryo</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Endosperm" title="Endosperm">endosperm</a> dominates and provides most of the <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a>. The storage <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">proteins</a> of the embryo and endosperm differ in their <a href="/wiki/Amino_acid" title="Amino acid">amino acid</a> content and physical properties.  For example, the <a href="/wiki/Gluten" title="Gluten">gluten</a> of wheat, important in providing the <a href="/wiki/Elasticity_(physics)" title="Elasticity (physics)">elastic</a> property to bread <a href="/wiki/Dough" title="Dough">dough</a> is strictly an endosperm protein.
</p><p>Seeds are used to propagate many crops such as cereals, legumes, <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forest trees</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turfgrass" title="Turfgrass">turfgrasses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pasture</a> grasses. Particularly in developing countries, a major constraint faced is the inadequacy of the marketing channels to get the seed to poor farmers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Thus the use of farmer-retained seed remains quite common.
</p><p>Seeds are also eaten by animals (<a href="/wiki/Seed_predation" title="Seed predation">seed predation</a>), and are also fed to <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> or provided as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birdseed" title="Birdseed">birdseed</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poison_and_food_safety">Poison and food safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Poison and food safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:Plant_toxins" title="Category:Plant toxins">Category:Plant toxins</a></div>
<p>While some seeds are edible, others are harmful, poisonous or deadly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>  Plants and seeds often contain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical_compounds" title="Chemical compounds">chemical compounds</a> to discourage <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbivores" title="Herbivores">herbivores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seed_predation" title="Seed predation">seed predators</a>.  In some cases, these compounds simply taste bad (such as in <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">mustard</a>), but other compounds are toxic or break down into toxic compounds within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digestive_system" title="Digestive system">digestive system</a>.  Children, being smaller than adults, are more susceptible to poisoning by plants and seeds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>A deadly poison, <a href="/wiki/Ricin" title="Ricin">ricin</a>, comes from seeds of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castor_bean" title="Castor bean">castor bean</a>.   Reported lethal doses are anywhere from two to eight seeds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
though only a few deaths have been reported when castor beans have been ingested by animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition, seeds containing <a href="/wiki/Amygdalin" title="Amygdalin">amygdalin</a> – <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apricot" title="Apricot">apricot</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bitter_almond" title="Bitter almond">bitter almond</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-almond_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-almond-63">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peach" title="Peach">peach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plum" title="Plum">plum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherry" title="Cherry">cherry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quince" title="Quince">quince</a>, and others – when consumed in sufficient amounts, may cause <a href="/wiki/Cyanide_poisoning" title="Cyanide poisoning">cyanide poisoning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-almond_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-almond-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>
Other seeds that contain poisons include <a href="/wiki/Annona" title="Annona">annona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Custard_apple" title="Custard apple">custard apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Datura" title="Datura">datura</a>, uncooked <a href="/wiki/Durian" title="Durian">durian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_chain" title="Golden chain">golden chain</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horse-chestnut_(tree)" title="Horse-chestnut (tree)">horse-chestnut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delphinium" title="Delphinium">larkspur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Locoweed" title="Locoweed">locoweed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lychee" title="Lychee">lychee</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nectarine" title="Nectarine">nectarine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rambutan" title="Rambutan">rambutan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosary_pea" title="Rosary pea">rosary pea</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sour_sop" title="Sour sop">sour sop</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_apple" title="Sugar apple">sugar apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wisteria" title="Wisteria">wisteria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taxus" title="Taxus">yew</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>  The seeds of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strychnine_tree" title="Strychnine tree">strychnine tree</a> are also poisonous, containing the poison <a href="/wiki/Strychnine" title="Strychnine">strychnine</a>.
</p><p>The seeds of many legumes, including the common bean (<i><a href="/wiki/Phaseolus_vulgaris" title="Phaseolus vulgaris">Phaseolus vulgaris</a></i>), contain proteins called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lectins" title="Lectins">lectins</a> which can cause gastric distress if the beans are eaten without <a href="/wiki/Cooking" title="Cooking">cooking</a>.  The common bean and many others, including the <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybean</a>, also contain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trypsin_inhibitors" title="Trypsin inhibitors">trypsin inhibitors</a> which interfere with the action of the digestive enzyme <a href="/wiki/Trypsin" title="Trypsin">trypsin</a>.  Normal cooking processes degrade lectins and trypsin inhibitors to harmless forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_uses">Other uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Other uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">Cotton</a> <a href="/wiki/Fiber" title="Fiber">fiber</a> grows attached to <a href="/wiki/Gossypium" title="Gossypium">cotton plant</a> seeds. Other seed fibers are from <a href="/wiki/Kapok_tree" title="Kapok tree">kapok</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milkweed" title="Milkweed">milkweed</a>.
</p><p>Many important nonfood oils are extracted from seeds. <a href="/wiki/Linseed_oil" title="Linseed oil">Linseed oil</a> is used in paints. Oil from <a href="/wiki/Jojoba" title="Jojoba">jojoba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crambe" title="Crambe">crambe</a> are similar to <a href="/wiki/Whale_oil" title="Whale oil">whale oil</a>.
</p><p>Seeds are the source of some medicines including <a href="/wiki/Castor_oil" title="Castor oil">castor oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea_tree_oil" title="Tea tree oil">tea tree oil</a> and the quack cancer drug <a href="/wiki/Amygdalin" title="Amygdalin">Laetrile</a>.
</p><p>Many seeds have been used as <a href="/wiki/Bead" title="Bead">beads</a> in necklaces and rosaries including <a href="/wiki/Job%27s_tears" title="Job's tears">Job's tears</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinaberry" title="Chinaberry">Chinaberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abrus_precatorius" title="Abrus precatorius">rosary pea</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castor_bean" title="Castor bean">castor bean</a>. However, the latter three are also poisonous.
</p><p>Other seed uses include:
</p>
<ul><li>Seeds once used as weights for <a href="/wiki/Weighing_scale" title="Weighing scale">balances</a>.</li>
<li>Seeds used as toys by children, such as for the game <a href="/wiki/Conkers" title="Conkers">Conkers</a>.</li>
<li>Resin from <i><a href="/wiki/Clusia" title="Clusia">Clusia</a> rosea</i> seeds used to caulk boats.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nematicide" title="Nematicide">Nematicide</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milkweed" title="Milkweed">milkweed</a> seeds.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cottonseed_meal" title="Cottonseed meal">Cottonseed meal</a> used as animal feed and <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizer</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seed_records">Seed records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Seed records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Female_coco_de_mer_seed.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="1740" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Female_coco_de_mer_seed.jpg/220px-Female_coco_de_mer_seed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Female_coco_de_mer_seed.jpg/330px-Female_coco_de_mer_seed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Female_coco_de_mer_seed.jpg/440px-Female_coco_de_mer_seed.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Female_coco_de_mer_seed.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The massive <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coco_de_mer" title="Coco de mer">coco de mer</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Oldest_viable_seed" title="Oldest viable seed">oldest viable</a> <a href="/wiki/Carbon-14" title="Carbon-14">carbon-14</a>-dated seed that has grown into a plant was a <a href="/wiki/Judean_date_palm" title="Judean date palm">Judean date palm</a> seed about 2,000 years old, recovered from excavations at <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">Herod the Great</a>'s palace on <a href="/wiki/Masada" title="Masada">Masada</a> in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. It was germinated in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> (A reported regeneration of <i><a href="/wiki/Silene_stenophylla" title="Silene stenophylla">Silene stenophylla</a></i> (narrow-leafed campion) from material preserved for 31,800 years in the <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberian</a> <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a> was achieved using fruit tissue, not seed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>)</li>
<li>The largest seed is produced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coco_de_mer" title="Coco de mer">coco de mer</a>, or "double coconut palm", <i>Lodoicea maldivica</i>.  The entire <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a> may weigh up to 23 kilograms (50 pounds) and usually contains a single seed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li>The smallest seeds are produced by epiphytic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchids" title="Orchids">orchids</a>. They are only 85 micrometers long, and weigh 0.81 micrograms. They have no <a href="/wiki/Endosperm" title="Endosperm">endosperm</a> and contain underdeveloped embryos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>The earliest <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">fossil</a> seeds are around 365 million years old from the <a href="/wiki/Famennian" title="Famennian">Late</a> <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>.  The seeds are preserved immature <a href="/wiki/Ovule" title="Ovule">ovules</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plant</a> <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Elkinsia_polymorpha&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Elkinsia polymorpha (page does not exist)">Elkinsia polymorpha</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_religion">In religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: In religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a> in the Old Testament begins with an explanation of how all plant forms began:
</p>
<blockquote><p>And God said, Let the earth bring forth grass, the herb yielding seed, and the fruit tree yielding fruit after his kind, whose seed is in itself, upon the earth: and it was so. And the earth brought forth grass, and herb yielding seed after its kind, and the tree yielding fruit, whose seed was in itself, after its kind: and God saw that it was good. And the evening and the morning were the third day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> speaks of seed germination thus:
</p>
<blockquote><p>It is <a href="/wiki/Allah" title="Allah">Allah</a> Who causeth the seed-grain and the date-stone to split and sprout. He causeth the living to issue from the dead, and He is the one to cause the dead to issue from the living. That is Allah: then how are ye deluded away from the truth?<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seed&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1093669538">.mw-parser-output .portalbox{padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portalborder{border:solid #aaa 1px}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:175px;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portalborder>ul{padding:0.1em;background:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style><div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint plainlist portalbox portalborder tright" role="navigation">
